interest rate for LIBOR-based US dollar single currency loans, and an IDA credit of SDR
17.4 million ($25 million equivalent) at standard terns with 35 years' maturity. The
borrower would be the People's Republic of China.






- 59-                      ANNEX I
ANNEX 1: BACKGROUND TO YUNNAN PROVINCE AND
PROJECT CITIES
1.    Yunnan Province is located in southwest China and is bordered, clockwise from the
north, by the following: the Provinces of Sichuan and Guizhou, Guangxi Zhuang
Autonomous Region, the countries of Viet Nam, Lao PDR and Myanmar, and Tibet
Autonomous Region. The northwestem area has a temperate climate, being dominated by
the southeastern Himalayas, where the upper reaches of three great rivers (the Jingshajiang,
which discharges to the Changjiang [Yangtze]; the Lancangjiang [Mekong]; and the
Nujiang [Salween]) flow southward barely 80 km apart. In contrast, the southern areas are
tropical, while central and eastern areas comprise a plateau of red earth and lake basins at an
elevation of about 2,000 m, and have a subtropical climate. The source of the Nanpanjiang
(Pearl River) is in the northeast of the Province. The average annual rainfall is between 800
and 1,000 mm, with low precipitation in the northwest, high in the southeast; 60 percent of
the rainfall occurs from June to August. The average temperature is 8 to 170C in January;
1 I to 29C in July.
2.    Yunnan Province has a total land area of about 394,000 km2 and a population of
some 38 million, of which about 15 percent live in urban areas. The Province has the
largest number (23) of nationalities in China. It is the third poorest, with a 1992 per capita
gross domestic product (GDP) of Y 1,165 ($134). Over 85 percent of the population earn
their living from the land, but Yunnan's mountainous terrain leaves only 6 percent of the
land with a slope of less than 15 percent. Despite difficult growing conditions, agriculture
managed a respectable 5.4 percent growth rate from 1980 to 1992; however this was
insufficient to fully employ the agricultural labor force which, as elsewhere in China,
remains much in excess of requirements. In recent years, underemployed rural labor has
taken advantage of new freedom of movement to seek work in the industrial and service
sectors that are themselves concentrated in urban areas.
3.    Industry employs only 7 percent of the 20 million strong labor force. It grew at an
average rate of 11.1 percent a year from 1980 to 1992, and now accounts for 41.1 percent of
Yunnan's GDP. The service sector has grown even faster, at 11.5 percent a year over the
same period, and now contributes 17.7 percent of GDP, employing 13.5 percent of the labor
force. Improvements in provincial road and rail transport, with an attendant lowering of
travel costs, and the opening up of international borders with Viet Nam, Lao PDR and
Myanmar, should all help sustain momentum for industrial, service and urban growth over
the near term.



- 60 -                     ANNEX 1
Gejiu
4.    Gejiu Municipality comprises an area of 1,876 km2 and a population of 337,000.
Gejiu City, a tin and nonferrous metal industry city of some 134,000 situated in a mountain
valley, evolved from the discovery and exploitation of tin. Its primary source of industrial
water is Lake Gejiu, which suddenly appeared in 1954 after unusually heavy rains. Gejiu
City faces a situation of too much water/flooding during the wet season and too little water
during the dry season. Drinking water is piped from a reservoir above the city because
Lake Gejiu has been polluted to Grade 5 by soil erosion, waste ore-dressing water and
tailings, urban garbage and sewage, and industrial wastewater. Water volume has been
reduced from 5.6 million m3 on formation of the lake to 3.2 million m3 in 1994 as a result of
soil erosion caused by the steady stripping of the extremely steep mountainsides since 1958
for either forage/firewood or mining activities, and sludge buildup.
Kunming
5.    Kunming Municipality is the capital and economic center of Yunnan Province,
dominating all other cities in both population and economic activity. The population of
Kunming Municipality was reported at 3.6 million in 1992 with about 1.2 million (about 33
percent) living in the urban areas and 2.4 million residing in the country areas. Kunming is
a multiminority city with minority groups representing some 12 percent of the population.
The municipal population is expected to reach about 3.9 to 4.2 million by year 2000 with
some 2 million in the urban area.
6.    There are some 5,000 industrial enterprises located in Kunming, including
machinery, metallurgy, electrical power, building materials, food processing, chemical and
textile industries. Many of the industries were established more than 50 years ago.
Kunming's growth provides jobs for rural migrants and increasing demand for a wide
variety of agricultural products and industrial raw materials produced in the rural areas.
Investments in infrastructure have not kept pace with the needs.
7.    The development of the city has been somewhat uneven. The first master plan for
the city was produced in 1980 and revised in 1987. The 1987 Plan is currently under
revision.
Water Supply
8.    The first water supply for Kunming dates back to 1915. Since that time, additional
sources have been developed. Up to about 1962 groundwater abstraction from the
limestone formations underlying Kunming provided the supply for the city, reported at
about 130,000 m3/day at that time. Since the early 1960s the city has relied almost wholly
on surface water supplies. The two main sources are the Songhuaba Reservoir on the
Panlong River, 13 km northeast of Kunming, and Dianchi Lake. Operational responsibility
rests with the Kunming Water Supply Company (KWSC) which reports through the Public
Utilities Bureau to the Construction Commission. Five treatment plants, with a total
capacity of 410,000 m3/day, have been built and commissioned over the years, the most



- 61-                      ANNEX 1
recent being the No. 5 Plant, which was commissioned in 1990. As designed, about 50
percent of the raw water is abstracted at each source. However, the sources are operated
conjunctively, with preference being given to drawing excess water from the Songhuaba
reservoir since this water quality meets the Grade II National Environmental Quality
Standard for Surface Water. The reservoir embankment has recently been raised to increase
the storage from 70 million m3 to 230 million m3, primarily for purposes of flood control,
but the water supply availability is increased to 300,000 m3/day (from 224,000 m3/day).
9.    In addition to the abstraction from  Dianchi Lake for water supply, some
200,000 m3/day is withdrawn for industry and agriculture.  Future water availability
depends on water balance analyses yet to be completed.
10.   The following issues need to be addressed relating to water quality, quantity and
reuse from Dianchi Lake.
Sewerage and Drainage
11.   Kunming drains naturally toward the Dianchi Lake with the Panlong River and
many small streams and canals feeding into the lake from the northern side of the city. The
city center has developed on flat low-lying land with consequent problems for the drainage
of stormwater and wastewater flows. Construction of a combined drainage system started
in the 1950s, mainly in the city center. The canals are still used to a large extent in outlying
areas. Sewerage operation and maintenance is very fragmented at present, there being
urgent need for a consolidated organizational arrangement covering the whole service.
12.   A Sewerage Master Plan was prepared in the late 1980s and approved by
government in 1991. The planning horizon of the SMP is year 2000 and the dry-weather
wastewater flow at that time was estimated at 643,000 m3/day. Over the years a number of
pumping stations have been constructed (nine for sewage and nine for storm flows). About
135 km of pipelines have been built and some 130 km of canals and ditches are used in the
system. There is an apparent lack of overall planning, and the provisions do not seem to
have been developed within any longer-term overall drainage strategy, but seem to respond
to new developing areas in a haphazard way. Seven separate drainage systems have been
identified, each with its individual treatment facility, comprising the areas of Xin, Yunliang,
Chuanfang, Mingtong and Jiancao, Jinzhi, Baisha and Baoxiang, and Haigeng. Only two
sewage treatment plants, with design capacities of 55,000 and 100,000 m /day, are so far
operational. The proposed total capacity of these various facilities is about 550,000 m3/day,
although the basis of this estimate needs to be clarified.
13.   Wastewater issues that need to be addressed include:
(a)   The development of a comprehensive long-term master plan and wastewater
strategy for wastewater collection, treatment and disposal, and a phased
investment program based on the least-cost, sustainable development
options;



- 62 -                      ANNEX 1
(b)   Development of realistic design criteria for wastewater treatment design,
based on current disposal arrangements in Yunnan, where septic tank
treatment is widely adopted, and considering site-specific raw water analysis
and data;
(c)    Cost effectiveness and practicality of providing separate sewer systems in
existing developed areas; and
(d)   The need to determine and put in place the most effective institutional
arrangements for operation and maintenance of sewerage operations city
wide, in terms of financial and operational viability.
Solid Waste Management
14.   Solid Waste Management operations are theoretically decentralized to the district
level under the District Administrative Governments, although the decision-making
continues to be taken largely by the Municipal Environmental Sanitation Section (this
section runs the new landfill sites). Firm data on solid waste operations is scant; Kunming
Municipal Environmental Sanitation Section records indicate that some 334,000 tons/year
of solid waste and 233,000 tons/year of nightsoil were dealt with during 1993. The solid
waste collection fleet comprises about 65 vehicles of two-ton capacity and an equal number
of five-ton capacity. Some 100 vacuum tankers are deployed to deal with the nightsoil.
Disposal of solid waste is to various landfill sites around the city. Current disposal is at half
a dozen uncontrolled dumps on the periphery of the city. Future disposal will be at two
landfills to be developed as part of this project.
15.   Nightsoil has traditionally been disposed of as fertilizer in agricultural areas, but this
outlet is reducing as farmers are becoming reluctant to take nightsoil, preferring to use
chemical fertilizer now becoming available. As a result a large proportion of nightsoil and
sludge from the septic tanks is now deposited in the lake or mixed with the sewage for
treatment prior to being discharged to the lake. The long-term strategy to be adopted to deal
with this issue is to phase out septic tanks.
16.   There seems to be no regulation of hazardous waste in Yunnan Province, although a
proposal for a "Solid Waste Pollution Control and Prevention Law" is expected to be
approved in late 1994. Classification of categories of .solid waste is urgently needed,
hazardous waste classification being particularly unclear.
Qujing
17.   Qujing Municipality comprises an area of 4,350 km 2 and a population of 220,000.
Qujing City is the second-largest city in Yunnan after Kunming, with an area of 13.5 km2
and a current population of about 161,500. It has been targeted by provincial authorities as
an open city, with foreign investment strongly encouraged. Its population is projected to
reach 340,000 by the year 2000 and 550,000 by 2010. The city is situated on the
Nanpanjiang, source of the Zhujiang (Pearl River). Qujing is a water-short area; water is



- 63 -                      ANNEX 1
provided to the city from two reservoirs, and in recent years there has been conflict between
these two sources of demand. In addition, some industries are extracting groundwater for
their own use, depleting the groundwater supply enough to cause land subsidence in some
areas. There is little treatment of domestic and industrial wastewater. The Qujing portion
of the Nanpanjiang exceeds Grade V of the Chinese national water standards, seriously
affecting the life of the river and that of the Zhujiang, and the well-being of the people and
cities along their banks.



- 64 -                     ANNEX2
ANNEX 2: DETAILED PROJECT DESCRIPTION
Background
1.    Yunnan Province lies in the southwest corner of China. The province has a
population of about 38 million, and is one of the poorest in China, with large numbers of
the rural population living below the official poverty level. Many major rivers pass through
Yunnan providing ample water resources at the provincial level. Although Yunnan is
predominantly a rural province, the urban areas of Kunming, Qujing and other centers have
been growing rapidly over the last two decades, experiencing migration from rural areas and
other provinces.
2.    The province has undergone rapid industrialization as government at all levels has
sought to broaden the mainly agricultural economic base. This has been achieved through a
strategy of processing the many agricultural products, prior to export, and exploiting the
province's large mineral resources such as tin, phosphates and coal. Industrialization has
occurred in both rural and urban areas, with large processing factories, such as steel
smelters, being established within the city limits, and many small-scale township and
village enterprises (TVEs) set up in rural areas. As a result, the provincial gross domestic
product (GDP) has grown at a rate of over 10 percent per year over the last decade.
3.    The benefits of this recent economic expansion have also resulted in serious
environmental degradation.  Urban redevelopment, funded by increased wealth, and
industrialization have increased water demand substantially. In these areas, traditional
nightsoil collection has been replaced with sewerage systems, while yard taps have been
replaced with indoor multifaucet connections allowing increasing use of washing machines
and other water-using appliances, consistent with increasing prosperity of the urban
dwellers. This has resulted in ever-increasing demands for expanded water supply systems,
and consequent discharge of untreated domestic and industrial wastewater into water
courses due to inadequate collection and treatment facilities. The generation of solid waste
in urban areas is increasing rapidly, particularly packaging, plastic and other
noncompostable materials associated with rising income levels. In particular, industrial
waste, containing toxic and hazardous materials, poses a major disposal problem. At
present, domestic and industrial waste is disposed not to sanitary landfills but to
uncontrolled dump sites and part composted, resulting in hazards to farmers, and pollution
of watercourses from leachate seepage from the dump sites.
4.    This project focuses on three areas in Yunnan where the economies and
environmental conditions particularly reflect the situation outlined above. These are (a) the
Lake Dianchi Basin Catchment, which includes Kunming, the largest city in the province
and the political and commercial capital of Yunnan; (b) Qujing city; and (c) Gejiu city.



- 65 -                      ANNEX2
5.    Kunming is located at the north end of Lake Dianchi. Although Yunnan is rich in
water resources, the Dianchi catchment is a water-scarce area. Ever-increasing domestic
and industrial demands cause conflict with existing agricultural and irrigation water uses.
Kunming draws its water supply in part from Lake Dianchi and partly from the Songhuaba
reservoir, which was originally built to serve irrigation demands in areas to the north and
east of Kunming city. At present most of the domestic wastewater from Kunming's 1.2
million residents, together with industrial wastewater flows, is discharged largely untreated
into Lake Dianchi through various streams and watercourses flowing through the city areas.
As a result, the lake has become polluted and eutrophication is occurring, caused by
excessive nutrient discharges (mainly phosphorus and nitrogen). These nutrients originate
from domestic sewage and certain industrial activities, such as fertilizer production. Two
large fertilizer factories, situated at the south end of the lake are major contributors of
phosphorus to the lake. This deterioration in water quality in the lake is such that one of the
city's water works has been closed down due to the poor water quality. Songhuaba
catchment, which now provides more than 50 percent of Kunming's water supplies, is being
used increasingly for high-intensity agricultural and industrial activities. Protection of this
catchment is also important to prevent degradation of the water quality in the reservoir and
safeguard this water resource for Kunming.
6.    The Yunnan Provincial Government has recognized the need to halt and reverse this
environmental decline and has initiated various actions to address this issue. Environmental
Protection Bureaus at all levels of government, established in line with central government
mandates, have initiated monitoring of environmental conditions and regulation of
industrial discharges. In addition, Kunming Municipality has established a Lake Dianchi
Protection Committee.
7.    The Caohai, or inner Lake Dianchi, which accounts for 2.5 percent of the lake area,
receives about 50 percent of Kunming's wastewater, and is seriously polluted. The Caohai
has recently been separated from the outer lake (the Waihai) by an earthen bund which is
fitted with control gates, and a 4.5 km long tunnel (Xiyuan Tunnel) constructed to discharge
water from the Caohai to a tributary of the Tanglangchuan River. The objectives of this
construction are (a) to increase the flood protection capacity of the lake; and (b) to prevent
polluted water from the Caohai from entering the main outer lake water body.
8.    Actions have been taken to substitute Songhuaba water with Dianchi water for
irrigation uses, thus freeing more higher-quality water from Songhuaba reservoir for
Kunming's water supply. Demand management measures have been initiated, including the
establishment of a Water Savings Office to help reduce wastage and unaccounted-for water.
Domestic solid waste collection is reasonably effective in the city's central areas but needs
to be expanded to include the suburban areas.
9.    Qujing lies on the Nanpanjiang River, which is a tributary of the Pearl River system,
about 120 km northeast from Kunming. The city is the second largest in the province, with
a current population of about 161,500, and is expanding rapidly with an anticipated
population of some 570,000 by year 2020. The area is rich in natural resources with many



- 66 -                     ANNEX2
industries established in and around Qujing including chemical, metal processing, textiles,
plastics, tobacco and automobile industries. The environmental problems in Qujing are
similar to those experienced by Kunming, resulting from inadequate municipal
environmental services that have failed to keep pace with the urban growth.
10.   Gejiu city is located some 300 km to the southeast from Kumning, has a present
population around 134,000. This figure is expected to reach some 180,000 by the year
2020. The city has developed around Gejiu Lake, which was formed some 50 years ago as
a result of flood events. The economy of Gejiu depends almost entirely on tin mining and
processing activities in and around the city.
11.   The proposed project will include both immediate interventions to reduce
environmental pollution and longer-term initiatives to support a sustainable and equitable
framework for economic growth. There is urgent need to halt and reverse the current
downward spiral of environmental degradation in the selected urban areas. Achieving
sustainable and equitable development requires a blend of integrated institutional, financial
and technical actions. The specific objectives of the project are to (a) strengthen policies,
regulations, and institutional arrangements for pollution control, municipal wastewater,
solid waste and nightsoil management; (b) support the improvement of the lakes
environment in Gejiu and Kunming in order to allow the waters to be used for domestic and
industrial supply and in agriculture; (c) support complimentary investments in pollution
control and municipally-provided urban environmental services; and (d) introduce a
comprehensive approach to planning, prioritization, and financing of urban environmental
infrastructure investments.
A. DIANCHI BASIN MANAGEMENT
Kunming
Kunming Municipal Solid Waste Management
12.   Kunming, the province's major city , is rapidly developing; its older, urban center is
under massive redevelopment; and its suburbs are continually expanding. Its current
population is approximately 1.2 million, which according to the city's Master Plan is
expected to increase to 2.2 million by 2005. The collection of solid waste in the city's
urban districts is being carried out in a satisfactory manner, but collection in suburban
districts is constrained by a lack of vehicles, fewer staff and longer collection distances.
Disposal of the city's 9,000 tpd (1,000 tpd domestic, 8,000 tpd other) at seven informal
dump sites is the most pressing problem. In order for waste arrangement facility to be able
to cope with this growth, more efficient, long term solutions need to be developed.
Population and Solid Waste Generation Trends
13.   Kunming municipality consists of four major districts, two urban, Panlong and
Wuhua, and two peri-urban or suburban districts, Guandu and Xishan. Population densities
2
differ markedly ranging from approximately 8,000 inhabitants/kM  in Xishan to almost



- 67 -                      ANNEX2
35,000 inhabitants/km' for Panlong. The 1995 populations of Guandu and Xishan were
533,000 and 284,000, respectively. It is these areas that will experience the most growth in
the future with expected populations reaching 715,000 and 374,000, respectively, by 2005.
In contrast, the populations of Panlong and Wuhua are both close to 500,000, but they are
expected to grow by only some 16 percent by 2005. Currently most of the domestic,
market, and commercial wastes and street sweepings are collected in Panlong and Wuhua
but not in Guandu and Xishan. It is expected that annual waste generation will follow these
population trends.
14.   In 1993, the solid waste collection rates in the two urban districts were 870 tpd, and
for the two suburban districts only 86 tpd, indicating a low efficiency of collection in those
districts. A visit to these areas generally confirms that much of the waste is not collected
but thrown along the street or in drains. An estimate of this quantity is 400 tpd. On the
positive side, the most recent data (1994) suggests that some 1,032 tpd are being collected
in Kunming.
Waste Composition Trends
15.   The major expected trend in waste composition will be toward lower density as the
ash content decreases. In areas where coal is used as fuel, ash compromises almost
3
70 percent of the solid waste, resulting in a density of almost 600 kg/mi. In areas where gas
is used, there is a complete absence of ashes, resulting in a density of only 370 kg/mi. The
organic fraction (mainly kitchen residues) changes appreciably, representing only
20 percent in areas where coal is used but 75 percent in areas with gas. The corollary is that
the daily per capita waste generation in coal-burning areas is between 0.8 and 0.9 kg and in
those with gas it is 0.35. These trends will have a significant impact on the collection and
disposal system but for regional planning purposes, a figure of 0.5 kg/capita/d is still
frequently used.
Current Management Practices
16.   Existing Collection Methods.  There are several categories of daily waste
collection practices in Kunming. There is a combination of 220 liter bins (4,000 in
number); apartment house chutes into I mi3 bins; the use of concrete "vats" into which
residents deposit their refuse; and the use of compactor trucks on the "bell" system. Much
of the waste collected by handcarts and tricycles goes to eight small transfer stations (STS)
located in the urban areas. There are no transfer stations in the suburban districts of Guandu
and Xishan.
17.   Collection vehicles include a combination of handcarts (609), tricycles (214) and
close to 150 trucks, ranging in capacity from 0.45 to 5.0 tons. Many of the smaller vehicles,
bicycles and tricycles (0.45 to 2.0 tons) are operated in the urban areas with very few
vehicles working the suburban districts. Staff resources for collection total just over 3,000
for the two urban districts and approximately 400 for the suburban areas. Clearly, many of
the staff in the urban areas are street sweepers.



- 68 -                      ANNEX2
18.   Collection issues include a heavy reliance on manual labor, resulting in double
handling where bicycles and tricycles are involved without a unified container system. In
addition, the 220 liter bins have a life of only two years due to mechanical damnage and
corrosion; the 7 m3 containers used at the STSs appear to be too small; and compactor
trucks are not considered useful since the waste does not compact easily. A more important
point is that the efficiency of collection is low and some areas are either not served or
served badly.
19.   Current Disposal Methods. Disposal as currently practiced is haphazard, with
much of the waste dumped in open areas around the city. In Xishan and Guandu there is
evidence of extensive dumping in open areas and alongside rivers and roads. During the
last 10 to 15 years some 2.8 million tons have been dumped at seven sites around the city.
The two largest sites, Wanglonqing in the northwest and Laohuashan in the east have
received approximately 2.4 million tons. All these sites represent environmental hazards,
since there is leachate collection, compaction or daily cover. One of the objectives of this
project will be to close these sites.
Institutional Responsibilities
20.   Overall management responsibility for the collection and disposal of solid waste in
the Municipality of Kunming rests with the Kunming City Appearance Committee;
leadership and guidance is provided by the Kunming Municipal Environmental Sanitation
Section. This Section is developing the new landfills proposed for Kunming. The actual
collection and transfer of wastes to the dump sites is undertaken by the District
Environmental Sanitation Sections (DESS).
Strategies for the 21st Century
21.   As the population and suburban infrastructure of the city continue to grow, a new
and modem management approach to the solid waste problem needs to be taken. Major
investments are required, including transfer stations; a broad range of collection vehicles,
each suited to a specific purpose; heavy, large transfer vehicles; and state-of-the-art
landfills. The municipality has made a conscious decision to move in this direction with the
assistance of Bank/IDA financing for equipment and institutional investmnents. Investments
that are under consideration include low-technology collection vehicles such as tricycles,
minitrucks, rear-loading trucks; small and medium transfer stations; landfills and attendant
facilities; training; special studies and other types of institutional development activities.
22.   These modem solutions require significant capital expenditure and therefore require
cost recovery schemes. To date, very little revenue has been collected for domestic refuse
collection, but a new law (September 22, 1995) has been enacted authorizing the collection
of fees. The fee for household waste was established at Y 5 per household per month, to be
collected by the environmental sanitation department of the operating district. Enterprises
and government units will have to pay rates ranging from Y 60 to Y 70 per month, but it is
not clear if this is a flat or per ton charge. To date there are no plans for administrative units
to collect these fees and provide accounting and other financial services.



- 69 -                      ANNEX2
Recommended Collection and Transfer Approach
23.   Expected Waste Generation and Composition. The domestic waste collection
forecast for the year 2000 is some 1,512 tpd increasing to 1,646 tpd by the year 2005. The
fraction of households using gas is estimated to be about 70 percent in 2000 rising to almost
75 percent by 2005. However, the average per capita generation rate stays about the same,
between 0.45 and 0.49 kg, because per capita waste generation rises with expected
prosperity but falls with the increasing use of gas. The effects of these two factors appear to
be compensating. Discussions with urban planners and a willingness to pay survey carried
out by YEPO (August 1995) indicated that roughly 1,500 tons of domestic waste will be
collected in the year 2000.
24.   Vehicles and Containers Required. In order to deal with the above waste
quantities in the year 2000, trends in composition and source characteristics, the following
collection vehicles will need to be procured under this project (there are additional vehicles
needed, but they will be procured using local funds):
(a)   40, 2.5 t small compactor trucks
(b)   40, 12 m3 fore and aft trucks
(c)   26, 16 m3 container carrying trucks
(d)   22,24 m3 container carrying trucks
(e)   5, 1.7 m3 loaders at each MTS
(f)   5, mini-bus and cars at each MTS
(g)   52, 16 m3 containers
(h)   50, 24 m3 containers
Note: A large number of smaller bins and plastic containers will also be procured using
local funds.
25.   Transfer Stations Required. Small transfer stations (STSs) able to receive wastes
from cyclists and minitrucks are needed for many urban areas. As of November 1995,
some 8 STSs were in operation handling about 30 tpd during a 5- to 6-hour shift. The old
STSs have limited storage capacity and 13 new STSs are therefore recommended. These
new stations will be capable of handling 60 tpd through the use of 16 m3 bins that can easily
loaded directly on to trucks. These stations will collect some 600 tpd delivered by
minitrucks and the private sector, which will be transported directly to the landfills.
26.   Five new medium-size transfer stations (MTSs) will be required to receive wastes
from STSs and larger, rear-loading trucks. These stations would handle 900 tpd through
16 m3 containers as well, which could handle some 15,000 kg of refuse of density
600 kg/m3. These stations would be at sites outside the two urban areas so that they could
easily serve larger areas.
27.   In addition to the transfer stations, transfer trucks will be required. The existing and
new STSs will need 26 trucks capable of carrying 16 m3 containers. The new MTSs will
require 22 arm-roll trucks capable of carrying 24 m3 containers.



- 70 -                      ANNEX2
Recommended Disposal Approach
28.   Two major landfills are proposed under this project, the Honshuitang site, located
19 km to the northwest of Kunming, and the Baishuitang site located 20 km to the
southeast. These two locations were selected from some 25 sites within 30 km of Kunming
that were under consideration earlier in the project cycle. Honshuitang will receive about
600 to 700 tpd during its first phase of 11 years. Its effective volume is about 10 million m3
and it should have a life of 21 years. Baishuitang has the same effective volume and will
receive approximately 900 tpd during its first phase of 13 years. Its life has also been
estimated at 21 years.
29.   A minimum of infrastructure is already in place at Honshuitang, and geotechnical
investigations have begun and the site acquired. The Baishuitang site will be leased under a
30-year agreement for Y 150,000 annually.
Hongshuitang Landfill
30.   Site Characteristics. The Hongshuitang site has several geotechnical problems that
require resolution. The operational part of the site covers an area of approximately
0.65 km2 that will be developed in three phases. The site is bifurcated by a fault line
running north and south in a karst limestone area. The area has a number of karst fissures
and funnels that will be filled with a soil cement mix. The area is low to moderately hilly,
with a natural slope and change in elevation of about 115 m in the shape of an ellipse. It is
a recharge area for a perched aquifer with the flow in the direction of Songshanpu Spring.
However, the larger regional groundwater system does not appear to be affected by
precipitation falling on the site. The engineering geology includes slope deposited red clay
of varying depth throughout the site, at 2 to 5 m. Although the permeability coefficient
varies widely, a figure of 4.14xlO7 cm/sec is cited (ideal is 10- cm/sec), making it a
relatively favorable site. There also appears to be some seismic risk, which is prevalent
throughout the area. Detailed design features will be incorporated in order to take account
of this risk.
31.   Facility Design. The site will be developed in three phases, each constructed
separately and operated as needed over the life of the landfill. Three of the most critical
aspects of landfill design are the liner, leachate collection and treatment system, and a
surface water drainage system around the periphery of the site. The proposed liner includes
a 30 cm bottom clay layer, a geomembrane, 20 cm of coarse sand, a second geomembrane
topped with 10 cm of clay. The geomembrane will not be used throughout the site, in
critical areas where the natural clay liner is too thin. Based on the drawings, some 30
percent of the landfill will be lined with synthetic material. The leachate collection system
consists of a pattern of gravel drains inside a circular geotextile fabric. There will be no
leachate treatment system, but instead a retention pond or tank meeting first phase needs
with a volume of 20,000 m3. The leachate is to be recirculated through the landfill to be
absorbed and evaporated. The size of the pond has been calculated to meet needs during the
rainy season and therefore there should not be any net flow from the system. In order to



- 71-                      ANNEX2
prevent runoff from adjacent areas from entering the site a series of peripheral drains will
constructed. The flow will be drained without treatment via the Shalang River. Gas
coming from the landfill is to be collected via the vertical lines in the leachate collection
system and flared.
Institutional Strengthening
32.   A program of institutional strengthening would be undertaken in order that the
investments proposed will be sustainable over the long term and that the responsible
agencies will be able to meet continuing challenges. This program will consist of a study
on industrial and hazardous waste management in the Dianchi basin, technical assistance on
the development of improved collection vehicles, technical assistance for improved
management at municipal and district environmental sanitation sections; an impact
marketing study; and a regional solid waste management study.
33.   Proposed Component ($28.1 million). The proposed component would comprise
the following works:
(a)   Hongshuitang Landfill comprising site preparation and construction of a
new landfill with capacity of about 9 million (M) mi3 at a site some 19 km to
the northwest of the city, including leachate and gas collection/treatment
systems, site facilities and operational vehicles and plant.
(b)   Baishuitang Landfill comprising sitepreparation and construction of a new
landfill with capacity of about 10 Mm at a site some 20 km to the southeast
of the city, including leachate and gas collection/treatment systems, site
facilities and operational vehicles and plant.
(c)   Transfer Stations. Construction of about 18 transfer stations throughout
the city.
(d)   Collection and Transportation Vehicles.  Procurement of about 138
collection and tr;nsportation vehicles in sizes between 3 and 24 m3 capacity
and about 102 containers of 16 m3 and 24 m3 capacity.
(e)   Institutional Development and Training.  Provision of institutional
development and practical training for both management and operational
personnel, with particular attention being given to the control, management
and monitoring necessary for effective sanitary landfill operations.
Kunming Water Supply
34.   The present population provided with water supply from the municipal system in
Kunming is estimated around 1.49 million (84.5 percent of the total population). This
number is projected to reach 2.41 million in the year 2020, representing some 90 percent of
the total population projected at that time. Average water demand projections, based on



-72 -                      ANNEX2
gross per capita figures (covering domestic, commercial and industrial uses), ranging from
305 I/c/d in 1995 to 355 lIc/d in 2020, are estimated around 538,000 m3/d in 1995 rising to
some 953,000 m3/d by year 2020. Peak demands are estimated at 619,000 and 1,096,000
m3/d respectively in 1995 and 2020, thus demonstrating a clear need to augment the
availability of fully treated water in the short term, to meet the demand forecasts.
35.   Water resources are presently drawn from Lake Dianchi, Songhuaba reservoir and
groundwater in the ratio 57:40:3 percent respectively. The Songhuaba reservoir built in
1958, was raised by 14.7 m in 1994 in order to increase storage for flood protection and
potable water use, although, as yet, the water level has not been raised to the new maximum
storage level due to resettlement and related issues that are not resolved. Alternative
proposals to reduce the area of land to be inundated at the upstream end of the reservoir are
included in this project.
36.   It is reported that in 1995 analyses of Songhuaba water indicate good quality
generally complying with Grade II of Chinese Standard 3838, apart from occasional high
manganese values. On the other hand, Lake Dianchi water quality has deteriorated
significantly over recent years, in the range Grade III to below Grade V of the standard. As
a consequence, the Kunming Water Supply Company (KWSC) decided to maximize the
use of water from the Songhuaba source. The existing treatment capacities and water
sources are summarized as follows:
Capacity                             Peak Demand, m3/d

37.   The treatment process adopted by KWSC for the good quality Songhuaba water
consists of chemically assisted flocculation, tube module settlement, rapid gravity filtration,



- 73 -                     ANNEX2
chlorination and storage. In the case of Lake Dianchi water, dissolved air flotation, dual
media filters, ozonation and powdered activated carbon are being provided at the WTP
No. 6B which is currently under construction.
38.   KWSC and its consultants evaluated a number of alternative strategies for the
augmentation of treated water supplies for Kunming, and selected the least cost option
based on conjunctive use of the Dianchi Lake and Songhuaba sources, maximizing the use
of the better quality Songhuaba resource.
39.   Under this project, the capacity of WTP No. 1 would be extended by 70,000 mr3/d
and the 100,000 m /d first phase of a new WTP at Beijiaochang would be provided. These
works would be supplied through a new 1,600 mm diameter pipeline from Songhuaba
reservoir. Thus the total treatment capacity for the city would be increased to around
765,000 m3/d, which would meet the 2005 average demand. The further expansion of
Beijiaochang works to 200,000 m3/d would be required to meet future demand. The project
includes the provision of distribution pipework and system connections and a storage
reservoir of 10,000 m3 capacity for treated water, located on high ground some 4 km to the
west of Beijiaochang.

(f)   Metering and Equipment of Unaccounted-for Water Management
comprising flow/pressure measuring, leak detection, meters and related
equipment.

(g)   Songhuaba Reservoir Augmentation comprising facilities in connection

Kunming Wastewater
41.   A Sewerage Master Plan for Kunming was prepared with bilateral assistance and
approved in 1990. This plan, although somewhat overtaken by unplanned development, has
provided the basis for sewerage investments to date in Kunming.
42.   Wastewater flows from the central and suburban areas of Kunming have been
projected through 2020 (the adopted planning horizon), by considering various assumptions
for growth, access to sewer connections and water use projections. Based on the adopted
scenario, which is considered appropriate and consistent with the city development
projections, wastewater flows are projected to reach about 780,000 m3/d by 2020, with
rapid growth expected in the suburban areas. Details are summarized as follows:
Kunming Total Wastewater m3/d
1995           2000           2010           2020
City center        170,500        206,800        246,100         271,600
Suburbs                  -        181,100         361,100        508,500
Total           170,500         387,900        607,200        780,100
43.   Wastewater treatment in Kunming is limited to two sewage treatment works (Nos. 1
and 2) of capacity 55,000 m /d and 100,000 m3/d, which treat water pumped from an
adjacent river in the southern and eastern areas of the city. Further STWs (Nos. 3 and 4A
covering the northern and western areas of the city) are under construction. When
commissioned, these new works would increase the treatment capacity to about
210,000 m3/d, substantially below the projected need, even for the short term. Some
combined sewer systems cover the old downtown area, and at present most urban
wastewater is ultimately discharged to the Dianchi Lake, largely to the Waihai, contributing
to organic pollution of the lake and contributing a substantial proportion of the loads of
nutrients (nitrogen and phosphorus), thereby enhancing the lake eutrophication.
44.   An important focus of the wastewater treatment proposals is therefore the removal
of both nitrogen and phosphorus from the wastewater. This will be achieved by the design
of the activated sludge system proposed for all wastewater treatment plants to remove both
nitrogen and phosphorus. This involves a staged anaerobic, anoxic and aerobic activated
sludge process (the A20 process) to remove in the order of 75 percent of the phosphorus
and nitrogen loads.
45.   The project would support the construction of comprehensive interceptor sewer
systems throughout city and suburban areas to ensure that wastewater is conveyed to the



- 75 -                     ANNEX2
treatment locations. Additional wastewater treatment capacity of about 190,000 m3/d in
city and suburban areas would also be included, bringing the total capacity to around
545,000 m3/d at the end of the project. This would meet the anticipated need through year
2008 and beyond in the event that development and wastewater flows are below the
assumed projections.

Small Towns Wastewater
47.   This component comprises the collection, treatment and disposal of wastewater
from the county towns of Chenggong and Jinning, which lie in the catchment area of Lake
Dianchi. At present, the domestic and industrial wastewaters from both these towns
discharge directly into the lake, contributing significantly to the nutrient pollution of the
lake (3 to 6 percent of the total). The present population at Chenggong is reported about
30,000, this is expected to reach some 167,000 by year 2020 according to the Chenggong
County Master Plan. Wastewater flow projections for Chenggong estimate the flow at
about 15,000 m'/d in 2010, rising to about 30,000 m'/d by year 2020. The Jinning
population is reported about 30,000 at present, and projected to reach 80-100,000 by year
2020, with wastewater flows projected in the range 11,000 to 17,600 m3/d in 2010 and 2020
respectively.

Rural Sanitation
49.   Proposed Component ($2.3 million). The objective of this component is to
demonstrate appropriate wastewater treatment technology for replication in the rural areas
of the Dianchi and Songhuaba catchments. The project includes three pilot projects in the
villages of Dounan, Wulong and Xiaohe. Specifically, these pilot projects consist of
village-level wastewater collection and treatment systems, nightsoil and municipal solid
waste utilization, afforestation, drainage, farm-level environmental improvements and water
supply. The principal purpose of these investments is to provide a knowledge and empirical
base for the dissemination of affordable, village-level approaches to waste management.
50.   In Xiaohe the projects comprise: (a) the use of household-level anaerobic digesters
for nightsoil and animal waste disposal for the production of gas for cooking and lighting;
(b) afforestation of some 16,000 mu to reduce soil erosion; (c) improved agricultural waste
management practices; and (d) a collection system for domestic wastewater currently
polluting much of the village streets.
51.   In Dounan, the projects comprise: (a) a 30 tpd composting plant to compost the
community's municipal soil waste, with the compost being used as soil conditioner for
degraded, adjacent farmland; (b) improved agricultural waste management practices on
some 2,700 mu; (c) rehabilitation and expansion of a 500 m31d water supply system; and
(d) a low-cost wastewater collection and treatment system using a land treatment approach.
52.   In Walong the projects comprise:  (a) 1,000 household-level composters;
(b) improved agricultural waste management practices for some 3,000 mu; (c) a well-based
water supply system of 500 m3/d capacity; (d) a combined drainage system with primary
sedimentation; (e) a lotus pond wetland for treatment of the effluent coming from (d) above;
and (f) a hydroponic vegetable production system.
B. GEJIu
Wastewater Collection, Treatment and Disposal
53.   Gejiu Lake is a shallow lake, and was formned about 50 years ago through landslides
resulting from flood events at the time. Sewerage within Gejiu, a city with a population of
about 134,000, is a combined system discharging into the lake. Silt from tailing ponds
associated with tin mining and processing and runoff from deforested hillsides have added
to the problem of pollution in the lake. The water level in the lake has to be controlled to
avoid flooding within Gejiu; to prevent the adverse visual impact of low water levels. In
addition, the State Tin Corporation abstracts about 25 percent of its washwater requirements
from the lake.



- 78 -                      ANNEX2
54.   The Gejiu wastewater component is designed to address the pollution of the Gejiu
Lake, which is located immediately next to the central district of Gejiu, and accessible to
large numbers of residents. Due to the substantial quantities of untreated sewage currently
discharged to the lake, it is significantly polluted and the water quality has been
progressively degraded.
55.   The component provides for the collection, treatment and disposal of the wastewater
currently discharged to the lake, together with arrangements for pumping of flood flows
during the wet season to prevent flooding of low lying areas of the city, and provisions for
restoring the water balance during drought periods to maintain water levels for reasons of
amenity and water abstraction. The wastewater system includes interceptor sewers around
the lake shore; pumping of foul sewage and flood flows, high rate biological treatment of
foul sewage, prior to discharge to a river used for irrigation purposes, and facility to sustain
water balance of the lake. The improved water quality would enhance the amenity,
recreation and land use value of the surrounding area.
56.   Proposed Component ($7.9 million). The proposed component would comprise
the following works:
(a)   Interceptor and Conveyor Sewer Systems including about 3.7 km of
sewers ranging in size from about 600 to 800 mm diameter. Pump station
with a wastewater capacity of about 40,000 m 3/d and a stormwater capacity
of about 200,000 m /d. Wastewater conveyor of about 3.9 km length in
800 mm diameter force main and gravity sewer. Stormwater force main of
about 1,000 mm diameter, length 0.5 km.
(b)   Storm Drainage System including rehabilitation of existing culvert about
2.5 km long, and construction of about 1.3 km of concrete-lined tunnel of
size about 2.2 m high * 2.2 m wide, complete with integral wastewater
culvert.
(c)   Sewage Treatment Works comprising screens, grit removal facilities, high
rate activated sludge treatment with waste sludge stabilization and disposal,
and ancillary facilities for about 25,000 m3/d capacity.
(d)   Water Balance Facilities for Gejiu Lake comprising storage tanks of total
capacity about 1.5 MM3, for controlled release to Gejiu Lake (not financed
in this project).
C. QUJING
Municipal Solid Waste Management
57.   Qujing is a newly developing industrial city located about 150 km to the northeast
of Kunming. Much of the city was built in the last 10 years as a result of economic
development in the surrounding area. Infrastructure development has not kept pace.



- 79 -                     ANNEX2
Although the center of the city is clean and tidy, the peri-urban areas suffer from
indiscriminate dumping of waste. Approximately 200 tpd (between 170 and 220 tpd
depending on the season) are collected, representing roughly 80 percent of domestic waste
generated by a population of about 220,000. Authorities expect the solid waste quantities to
rise by 8 percent annually up to the year 2000 and by 5 percent up to the year 2010,
exceeding 400 tpd at the end of this period. As in Kunming, the increasing use of gas rather
than coal is moderating this projected increase somewhat in reducing the ash content of the
waste.
Overall Project Objectives
58.   The key objectives of the solid waste management programs in Qujing are:
(a)   Effective and efficient collection and disposal of domestic and industrial
solid waste, particularly in the suburban areas;
(b)   Safe disposal of hazardous wastes from industries and hospitals;
(c)   The reduction, reuse and recycling of waste;
(d)   The development of a disposal approach consisting of a system of transfer
stations and landfills;
(e)   The stabilization and closure of existing dumps; and
(f)   Improved operations and policy development through a program  of
institution building, training and developing approaches to enhanced cost
recovery for solid waste management services.
Population and Solid Waste Generation Trends
59.   From limited population trends and the growth of the sector during the early 1990s,
projections for solid waste generation in Qujing have been estimated. For the years 1991
through 1993, daily generation increased from 105 to 153 tpd. The unusually high growth
rate is primarily due to the incorporation of new areas into the Municipality of Qujing.
Based on the above growth rates, by 2000 waste generation will be 262 tpd and by 2005 it
will reach 335 tpd. The per capita generation at present is approximately 0.76 kg/d, much
of which is ash from coal burning.
Waste Compositional Trends
60.   Waste composition trends will be similar to that of Kunming in that the expected
rate of gas usage will increase to 40 percent in 2000 and to 73 percent in 2010 according to
the master plan for the city. The inorganic portion, primarily ash, will decline from 61
percent in 1995 to 20 percent by 2010. The per capita generation rate for the planning
period is expected to remain high despite the reduction of ash content, at 0.84 kg/d per



- 80 -                      ANNEX2
capita. This will also have a significant impact on refuse compactability, density and
landfill requirement.
Current Management Practices
61.   Current collection and disposal practices mirror those of Kunming, the center of the
city receiving a disproportionate amount of services compared to peri-urban areas. Of the
roughly 200 tpd of waste that are collected, 45 percent is collected by the Municipality and
the rest is delivered by a combination of trucks and handcarts from institutions and
commercial establishments. The collection of this waste is funded by the generators.
Sanitation staff number some 400 which include sweepers, collection people, drivers and
management personnel. There are over 1,000 refuse cans scattered throughout the city but
primarily in central areas. In addition, some 190 specialized refuse bins and 140 handcarts
are in use. As in Kunming, the collection system is highly manual with much double
handling. The Municipality operates 11 refuse trucks, four nightsoil pumping trucks and
five general-purpose small dump trucks.
62.   Disposal remains the principal issue in Qujing. Two dump sites located at the edge
of the city are used; a composting plant built in 1992 has now ceased to operate. Another
old dump site has been walled off and formally closed with the waste in place being
composted and sorted.
Institutional Responsibilities
63.   The principal government agency responsible for municipal solid  waste
management in Qujing is the Municipal Environmental Sanitation Office. The feasibility
study for the component mentions plans to create a separate transfer and disposal company.
To date nothing has been done to move the municipality in this direction. Therefore, it is
assumed that the major responsibility for implementing this component will remain with the
Sanitation Department.
Recommended Collection Approach
64.   Based on the analysis carried out, an entirely new approach to transfer and disposal
is recommended. Collection will basically be carried out as at present, with the exception
of improved coverage in the peripheral areas of the city. Transfer and disposal will
incorporate the use of six transfer station, five in Qujing proper and one in Zhanyi to the
north, and a sanitary landfill located between the two cities.
65.   Transfer Stations. Two small transfer stations will be built, each capable of
handling approximately 60 tpd. The distances to the new landfill are 2 to 3 km for the
station located in Qujing and 3 km for the one located in Zhanyi. In 1998, for example,
some 225 tpd will be collected and of this 60 percent will go through the transfer stations,
with the remaining amount going directly to the landfill. As the generation exceeds 400 tpd
around 2010, the transfer stations will have to accommodate 100 tpd. Initially, each transfer
station will be equipped with an 8-ton (16 m3)container carrying truck used for transfer



- 81-                       ANNEX2
purposes and one 5-ton rear-loading truck used primarily for direct collection and
subsequent discharge at the landfill. The dump trucks should be able to complete one round
trip to the landfill per hour and therefore dispose of roughly 50 tpd.
66.   Vehicles and Containers Required.
(a)   4, 8 t (14 m3 ) container carrying trucks
(b)   9, 5 t (8 m3 ) container carrying trucks
Recommended Disposal Approach
67.   Dagou/Xiaopo Landfill. A new landfill some 6 km northwest from Qujing city
center is proposed, located in a rear valley of Xiaopo Village and Taihe Mountain. The
volume of the landfill is 1,770,000 m3, which would suffice for 15 to 17 years depending on
such factors as landfill operations and refuse composition. The site is well situated in low
mountains and is basically in a V-shaped valley with about 150 m of relief. It is rocky and
the vegetation is sparse, basically scrub. Very little of the area is used for agricultural
purposes because of its low productivity and arid conditions. The site also has significant
clay, in some places as deep as 15 m, with permeability ranging from 10-2 to 104 cm/s,
which is much less than ideal.
68.   An access road will need to be built of some 1.5 km in length and a site road of
1.2 km is also needed in order to use the site completely during its two filling phases. Two
filling phases are required because of the unusual topography and severe slopes. Each
phase will last approximately seven to eight years and require construction of a leachate
control and landfill stabilization dam so that refuse can be worked on a horizontal surface.
A water control ditch will also be built around the site to catch and discharge runoff before
it has a chance to penetrate the fill.
69.   In order to control leachate, grouting methods will be applied and a synthetic liner
used. A leachate collection system similar to that being applied in the Kunming landfills
would be provided. There will be no direct treatment of leachate but a storage basin of
7,500 m3 capacity would be provided. Leachate would be recirculated through the landfill
or piped to a nearby wastewater treatment plant. Based on the current wastewater flow at
the treatrnent plant, the leachate would increase the flow only between 2 and 4 percent.
70.   A gas collection system is also being proposed to work in tandem with the leachate
collection system. The gas will be flared.
71.   Proposed Component ($4.5 million). The proposed component would comprise
the following works:
(a)    Dagou/Xiaopo Landfill comprising site preparation and construction of a
new landfill with capacity of about 1.8 Mm3 at a site some 6 km to the
northwest of the city, including leachate and gas collection/treatment



- 82 -                      ANNEX2
systems, site facilities and operational vehicles and plant, access and site
roads.
(b)   Transfer Stations. Construction of two transfer stations throughout the
city.
(c)   Collection and Transportation Vehicles.  Procurement of about 13
collection and transportation vehicles in sizes between 5 and 8 tons capacity.
(d)   Institutional Development and Training.  Provision of institutional
development and practical training for both management and operational
personnel, with particular attention being given to the control, management
and monitoring necessary to effectively operate sanitary landfill operations.
Wastewater Collection, Treatment and Disposal
72.   The primary objective of wastewater treatment for the city of Qujing is the
improvement of water quality in the Nanpanjiang, the quality of which is currently Class V.
The considerable variation in river flows means that dilution may be limited, and the longer
term objective is to provide secondary treatment of wastewater. The project will provide an
intermediate stage biological treatment, which can readily be incorporated in the longer
term facilities. Wastewater flows from the developed eastern and northern areas of the city,
will be intercepted and conveyed to the treatment site which is located to the south of
Qujing in the vicinity of the junction of the Baishi and Xiaoxianghe rivers. The trunk sewer
system and treatment facilities would be expanded in the future to accommodate the
wastewater flows from the western area of Qujing, which is expected to develop during the
next IO to 15 years.
73.   Proposed Component ($15.0 million). The proposed component would comprise
the following works:
(a)   Trunk Collector Sewer Systems including the construction of about
12.1 km of sewers in sizes between 300 and 1,800 mm diameter, including
sewer connections and related structures for interception of wastewater
flows from existing combined sewer systems and surface drainage channels.
(b)   Sewage Treatment Works comprising screens, pumping, grit removal,
intermediate biological treatment, sludge treatment and disposal, and
ancillary facilities, with capacity of about 80,000 m3/d.
(c)   Maintenance Depots, Sewer Cleaning and Safety Equipment for use
throughout the city, including bucket cleaning equipment, hoists,
transportation, and safety equipment to be based at maintenance depot at
STW site.



- 83 -                     ANNEX2
Water Supply
74.   Existing Situation. The combined population of Qujing and the satellite town of
Zhanyi (10 km to the north), was around 162,000 in 1992. This figure is projected to reach
437,000 and 452,000 in years 2010 and 2020, respectively. Average water demands are
estimated at about 66,500 m3/d in 1995, rising to 132,000 m3/d in 2010 and 153,000 m3/d in
2020. Peak values are estimated at 152,000 and 176,000 in years 2010 and 2020
respectively. Existing supplies, totaling 87,000 m3/d are obtained from Xiaoxiang, Xihe
and Niuguohe reservoir sources; however, the reliability of these sources is reported very
low in the range 35 to 45 percent. The installed treatment capacity at the existing three
works is reported around 81,000 m3/d. However, deficiencies in the existing distribution
system reduce the effective daily supply to around 55,000 m3/d.
75.   The proposed component in this project would: (a) provide improved distribution
pipework in the existing northern and eastern areas of the city to ensure distribution of the
full available supply of treated water from the existing works; and (b) address the apparent
supply deficiency by developing a new water scheme from the existing DuMu reservoir
which is located some 40 km to the northwest from Qujing. The DuMu source was selected
as the least-cost scheme to provide a reliable supply for the long term development of
Qujing, providing a safe yield (at 95 percent reliability) of 120,000 m3/d, which would
suffice to meet the peak demand through year 2020. The scheme would be developed in
two stages each of 60,000 m3/d capacity, the raw water main would be sized for the first
stage development and a duplicate pipe would be provided at a later date, since this is the
least-cost option for this pipeline (although the tunnel would be built for the full
development).
76.   Proposed Component ($21.2 million). The proposed component would comprise
the following works:
(a)   Distribution System Strengthening comprising pressure pipelines of steel,
ductile iron, or prestressed concrete materials, in sizes between 200 and
600 mm diameter, of about 19 km total length in the northern and eastern
areas of the city.
(b)   Raw  Water Transmission Pipeline comprising pressure pipeline of
prestressed concrete, steel, or other materials, about 1,000 mm diameter,
control valves and facilities, of about 34.1 km total length from DuMu
reservoir to Qujing, No.1 and No.2 WTP.
(c)   Extension of Water Treatment Plant No.2 at North Qujing comprising
flocculation, clarification, filtration, chlorination, storage, pumping and
ancillary facilities, of about 30,000 m3/d additional capacity.
(d)   Raw Water Transmission Tunnel. Horseshoe-shape pressure tunnel of
size about 2.0 m high * 2.0 m wide with reinforced concrete or spray
concrete lining, of about 9.3 km length.



- 84 -                     ANNEX2
D. INDUSTRIAL POLLUTION CONTROL
77.   The proposals for the Kunyang Phosphorus Fertilizer Factory comprise a
combination of process upgrading and wastewater treatment. The process upgrading will
permit production of higher grade products and will achieve improved water and materials
utilization. The reduced wastewater flow will be given treatment in the form of chemical
precipitation of phosphate to meet the standard for discharge to Dianchi Lake, which
requires a phosphorus concentration of not more than I mg/l in the treated wastewater. The
combined effect of the process upgrading and wastewater treatment proposals in an overall
reduction in the phosphorus load discharged to Dianchi Lake from 57 tons/year to less than
I ton/year, a reduction of about 98 percent. The wastewater discharge will be reduced from
540 m3/h to 117 m3/h.
78.   The proposals for the Kunming Chemical Fertilizer Factory are also based on a
combination of process upgrading and wastewater treatment. The process upgrading
proposals involve improvements in water recycling, recovery of ammonia and phosphate
chemicals and in desulfurization of the coal gas (produced on site by coal carbonization)
used in ammonia-based product manufacture. A new sulfuric acid plant using sulfur as raw
material is proposed to enhance phosphoric production, which is currently only internittent,
which causes high losses during startup and shutdown. The process improvements will
reduce wastewater discharges from 550 to 59 m3/h (ca 90 percent) and loads of ammonia
(as N) from 332 to 85 tons/year (about 75 percent) and phosphorus from 36 to 4 tons/year
(about 90 percent). Wastewater treatment will reduce these loads further to 10.6 tons/year
and 0.4 tons/year for ammonia (as N) and phosphorus respectively.
79.   Proposed Component ($34.1 million). The proposed component would comprise
the following works:
Kunyang Phosphorus Fertilizer Factory
(a)   a new 60,000 tons/year sulfuric acid production facility, which will enhance
production of downstream products and will allow a change from sulfide ore
to pure sulfur as a feedstock;
(b)   new circulating water systems and system refurbishment for industrial
phosphate production (100 m3/h); sulfuric acid plant (550 m3/h); chemical
fertilizer plant (150 m3/h); various other phosphate products (2 at 200 m3/h
and 2 at 20m3/h);
(c)   a new water treatment facility (300 m3/h);
(d)   improvements to intermediate wastewater treatment plant;
(e)   improvements to wastewater stream segregation; and



- 85 -                     ANNEX2
(f)    a new  wastewater treatment plant (150 m3/h) involving two-stage
precipitation and sedimentation and sludge treatment, and associated
laboratory facilities.
Kunming Chemical Fertilizer Factory
(g)   modifications to the coal gas cleaning, including sulfur recovery
(200 tons/year), and indirect cooling;
(h)   a new sulfuric acid plant (80,000 tons/year) using sulfur as feedstock;
(i)   upgrading of process water recycling in gas plant (by 270 m 3/hr); ammonia
synthesis (by 500 m 3/hr); phosphoric acid (200 m3/hr);
(j)   improvements to wastewater stream segregation;
(k)   wastewater treatment plant for phosphate removal by precipitation,
sedimentation and sludge treatment; and
(l)    wastewater treatment for nitrogen removal by nitrification, activated sludge,
secondary sedimentation and sludge treatment.
Environmental Pollution Control Subloans will be made for environmental
improvement measures of small-scale enterprises.  Subloan processing and
approvals will be covered by operational regulations to be issued shortly.
E. ENVIRONMENTAL MONITORING AND DATA MANAGEMENT
80.   Proposed Component ($6.2 million). The objective of this component is to
upgrade the facilities and strengthen the management of (a) the Yunnan Environmental
Monitoring Center; (b) the Kunming Environmental Monitoring Center; (c) the Honghe
Prefecture Environmental Monitoring Station; (d) the Gejiu Municipal Environmental
Monitoring Station; (e) the Qujing Prefecture Environmental Monitoring Center; (f) the
Qujing Municipal Environmental Monitoring Station; (g) the Yunnan Radiation Monitoring
Station Institute, and (h) Yunnan Environmental Management Institute. Specifically, the
project will help to improve the facilities in these centers and stations through upgrading of
existing laboratory buildings, including services and in particular the provision of stable
power supplies. Laboratory and field equipment, and computer hardware and software for
improved data management would be procured. There would also be provision for training
and technology transfer.
F. INSTITUTIONAL DEVELOPMENT, CONSTRUCTION SUPERVISION AND TRAINING
81.   Proposed Component ($19.1 million). The component would comprise a number
of main composite packages for the various executing agencies, covering institutional
development, construction supervision and training, as described below, together with an
allowance for support for provincial and sector city agencies, master planning, future



- 86 -                     ANNEX2
project preparation, and other programs of assistance to be further defined. Details are set
out below and in the Institutional Development, Construction Supervision and Training
Table, showing estimated national and international person-months and other supporting
related information. The scope of work and draft terms of reference for the main
assignments were reviewed by the Bank/IDA, and are in the Project File (see Annex 16).
Packages A to F: Institutional Development, Financial Management Improvement,
Construction Supervision and Training for Executing Agencies
Objectives
82.   The broad objectives of the main packages (A to F) are to:
(a)   strengthen the executing organizations in institutional and financial
management: water, wastewater, solid waste and nightsoil management,
and the related bureaus and divisions;
(b)   strengthen the overall provincial financial management and policy-making
in Yunnan; and
(c)   ensure the efficient implementation of the project while strengthening sector
institutions.
Scope of Work
83.   The services to be provided under these assignments are for substantial
multidiscipline support programs for the respective executing agencies and would include:
(a)   strengthening of organizations through development of appropriate
management procedures;
(b)   provision of improved accounting systems, management information
systems and training in water, wastewater, solid waste and nightsoil
management operations, and computer training for accounting staff;
(c)   water, wastewater, solid waste and nightsoil management utility pricing;
(d)   provincial financial management;
(e)   quality assurance training for materials production;
(f)   construction supervision;
(g)   solid waste management operations training;
(h)   wastewater treatment plant operations training;



- 87 -                     ANNEX2
(i)   skills upgrading for planning and analysis of development options; and
(j)   assistance to improve product technology.
Package G: Environmental Quality Monitoring and Data Management
Objective
84.   The objective of Package G component is to:
(a)   support the Environmental Monitoring and Data Management component of
the project, which involves refurbishment of existing laboratories and
provision of new analytical equipment to broaden the scope of
environmental monitoring in the Province; and
(b)   strengthen capabilities at both Provincial and Municipal in environmental
monitoring and data management to provide information that is of sufficient
quality to support the environmental decision-making process.
Scope of Work
85.   This package will provide practical training in the three stages of environmental
monitoring as follows:
(a)   sampling-design of sampling strategies and programs; sampling statistics;
sampling protocols;
(b)   analysis-design  and specification  of analytical programs; quality
assurance/quality control; and
(c)   data management-data storage; data retrieval; quality assurance/quality
control.
Package H: Training and Management Information Systems (MIS) Support
Objective
86.   The objective of Package H is to support the institutional development of project
entities and executing agencies through structured programs of "in-country" and overseas
training, and to support management information development.
Package I: Other
87.   The scope of work in Package I would include: water resources and drainage master
planning; equipment and support for Provincial and other Finance Bureaus; support for
Dianchi Lake Basin Authority; other related assistance and studies including wastes
management, and future project preparation.
